<div id="review_586197745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586197745" />
    <a title="Stephie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3621465-stephie"><img alt="Stephie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321767402p2/3621465.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586197745?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephie" href="/user/show/3621465-stephie">Stephie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer586197745&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586197745" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1509526796158633505">I feel like I'm maybe being a little bit generous in my rating. But I wasn't sure what to give this book (and really, series, as this book wraps everything up). <br/>I started reading this series a few years ago and then had to stop and wait for the rest. During that wait I got distracted with other books and kind of forgot about this. I decided to finish it, but decided to reread everything in case I forgot things. I'm glad I did as now everything is so fresh in my mind. <br/>So here goes. <br/>What I didn't </span>
  <span id="freeText1509526796158633505" style="display:none">I feel like I'm maybe being a little bit generous in my rating. But I wasn't sure what to give this book (and really, series, as this book wraps everything up). <br />I started reading this series a few years ago and then had to stop and wait for the rest. During that wait I got distracted with other books and kind of forgot about this. I decided to finish it, but decided to reread everything in case I forgot things. I'm glad I did as now everything is so fresh in my mind. <br />So here goes. <br />What I didn't like: <br />Schuyler and jack. I'm sorry. But I never liked them together. I always rooted for Oliver. When it became apparent that ship wasnt sailing anywhere (do you know how angry I was at reading Schuyler and Oliver together, only for them to break up?!) I tried to like Schuyler and jack. I really did. But I felt like their love came out of nowhere tbh. And I hated how they called each other "love" every five seconds. <br />The wolves and bliss. Don't get me wrong, I really liked bliss's character. It's just that I didn't realize I needed to read de la Cruz's wolf pack book in order to understand any part of bliss's chapters. Tied into this is the lack of the watcher. Perhaps she played a more important role in the wolf pack book? Idk. <br />Schuyler's genealogical work. I mean... Cool. I'm glad she discovered she had a half sister (which, wtf? Why? Just to give Oliver his own hea? More on that later...). And hooray! Schuyler has a loving grandma for once! Totally unfair to Cordelia who can't defend herself as she's made to look horrible for lying to the chase family about Allegra and Schuyler. <br />The entire EPIC BATTLE which wasnt epic at all. I'm sure in de la Cruz's mind it was. But the way the last part of the book was written was so quick as to be anticlimactic. Because there was no time to savor the feelings of each character as they thought they lost their loved ones. I was expecting more. Instead it was wham, bam, thank you ma'am...LUCIFER IS DEAD PRAISE JESUS! As a side note, did anyone else think it was weird how Jesus was never mentioned? For all the talk of lucifer being heaven's son, what about the other one? Wouldn't lucifer want to seek revenge on him more than anyone else? Religion man...idk<br />Gabrielle and Michael. Their entire storyline just made my skin crawl. I'm not sure i can put into words what really bugged me most. Maybe that they were supposed to be the uncorrupted, and yet Michael was pretty corrupt in his prideful ways. Add to that how he killed a lot of humans, lied to Gabrielle over and over, taking her memory. Then there was the big reveal that Michael could've killed lucifer but s love for Gabrielle stopped him and she was MAD about it? Did I read that part right? Maybe not because everything happened so fast...but it sure seemed that way to me. So let me get this straight. Love does not conquer all. At least, not romantic love. Which is fine. But the entire series revolves around Schuyler and jack and their love and finding a way blah blah blah. I'm getting off topic. I'm not even sure what I'm saying anymore. So. Schuyler leads the way back to the paradise and Gabrielle and Michael leave her? And what, are they together or...? I'm not sure what I'm supposed to think about them. Which is disappointing because I wanted a lot for them. It just didnt come through. There's a lot more i could say about them<br />We were given one line about the twins at the end, how each set lost one in the battle. I really liked both sets and wanted more. It was like Fred and George Weasley all over again. Only they weren't given enough space to properly mourn. <br />Jack...is he still a vampire or...<br />Oliver asked to be turned into a vampire. WHY. His familiar is a human. If we are to believe they are in love then why would he want to be immortal and she mortal. That's asking for heartache<br />What I did like:<br />Mimi and Kingsley. As soon as their potential was shown I was on board. I love Kingsley. And shockingly I love Mimi more than Schuyler. She was a far more interesting character than Schuyler. Had more layers, like and onion. She transforms herself over and over throughout the series. I never thought her as weak. Maybe spiteful, vindictive, but all understandable. And Kingsley, well, I just loved him. I loved his back story in Rome. Though I wish we could've seen his then unrequited love for azrael. <br />I'm glad everything came out. All the secrets and mysteries. One of my favorite things of this series was the use of the world's history, how everything was explained through the world of fallen angels. That was always the most interesting part for me, more important than the love stories. I only wish that the different aspects that came out in the end of the series, like the holy grail, had been given room to really grow into something more in depth. <br />Seeing those that had been consumed by silver bloods back in paradise. Dylan's character was so tragic and I initially hoped he'd somehow find a way back for bliss. But since he didnt, at least he was saved from the hell he was in. <br />Everyone got an hea in one way or another. <br />...<br />You'd think there'd be more? In the end I liked the books well enough, I suppose. I just wanted more, I guess. But for the most part, everything got tied up in a way that left me satisfied with the end for the fact that I'm not left wondering about so many things anymore. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1509526796158633505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_510021762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/510021762" />
    <a title="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish"><img alt="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405178063p2/5614985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/510021762?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" href="/user/show/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish">Hazel (Stay Bookish)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781423157410" href="/book/show/15818593-gates-of-paradise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=own-copy-read">own-copy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer510021762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2406721807173864528">I can't deny it. I have followed the blue bloods to hell and back. I have read them through seven books and it feels quite sad knowing this will be goodbye.<br/><br/>When I got my hands on the book, I felt relief and happiness wash through me because here it is finally, within my grasp, after a long long wait. I'm not a very patient person so you can only imagine what I had to endure. Soon though, when I got the book, I felt anxiety too. Because suddenly, I'm scared to reach the last page.<br/><br/>I've always enjo</span>
  <span id="freeText2406721807173864528" style="display:none">I can't deny it. I have followed the blue bloods to hell and back. I have read them through seven books and it feels quite sad knowing this will be goodbye.<br /><br />When I got my hands on the book, I felt relief and happiness wash through me because here it is finally, within my grasp, after a long long wait. I'm not a very patient person so you can only imagine what I had to endure. Soon though, when I got the book, I felt anxiety too. Because suddenly, I'm scared to reach the last page.<br /><br />I've always enjoyed the historical, mythological plot of the book so I found myself at ease when I was reading Gates of Paradise. As always, I commend Dela Cruz for her great imagination. I was never disinterested when it came to the series. The characters, are as they always are. Not much has changed. Mimi is still sassy, Kingsley is still smirky and gorgeous, Oliver is still adorkable. Bliss has come back after she's been long gone and now she brings new friends, new characters with her. I didn't read Wolf Pact so I wasn't able to know them well but I was still able to keep up.<br /><br />I however am quite disappointed about a few things. 1) Through the series, the way the characters speak have changed. I know they've matured from all the problems they've been through, but they talk like old people. I mean the way Schuyler and Jack call each other "my love" is quite sickening. They're what, eighteen? 2) For a finale of a series, I think the book was cut pretty short. This also caused the story being rushed. Gates of Paradise is supposed to be kick-ass action packed but it didn't seem so because everything went too fast and there wasn't much details. The big finale battle, which is the climax of a finale book, seemed insufficient. I wish there were more scenes. I wanted to see more of the couple's together too (Jack/Sky, Kingsley/Mimi and even Michael/Gabrielle). 3) The ending was frustrating!!!!!!!!!! It just blew my mind away so much because I never imagined such an open ended conclusion. I used to be accepting when it comes to these kinds of conclusion but I'm starting to hate them again. 4) Oh and did Schuyler really just detour to Chicago to find her family and attend a kegger when the entire blue blood community was being attacked? 5) I've always loved Oliver but the ending was disturbing (besides the fact it was open ended of course) 6) Have I mentioned how disappointed I am by how lithe the Kingsley/Mimi scenes are? (So not enough! They're always arguing or trying to kill each other. These two are my fave so is too much to ask for there to have been more?<br /><br />Still, there were some parts I liked/loved. The few sweet scenes Jack and Sky had together. Jack and Sky's ending. Oliver finding someone. The backstory of what happened in Rome. Adorable Kingsley/Mimi scenes.<br /><br />Yeah I was disappointed and now I feel hollow inside because the story ended but I still applaud Dela Cruz for her amazing series and for this final book. It has been a great ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2406721807173864528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_362996535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362996535" />
    <a title="Jeremy Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3177452-jeremy-martin"><img alt="Jeremy Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601340390p2/3177452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362996535?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeremy Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeremy Martin" href="/user/show/3177452-jeremy-martin">Jeremy Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3177452-jeremy-martin?shelf=originality-for-days">originality-for-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3177452-jeremy-martin?shelf=wish-it-was-better">wish-it-was-better</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362996535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9980221731464226978">This is the last book in the Blue Blood series. I have adored these books from the very first one. But as the series started to get further in number, the books started to lack their usual luster. Plots started to get shaky, and some things were simply forgotten. Some of the books were so cliche and typical that you felt angered that such a beautiful and interesting plot got ruined. <br/><br/>First complaint was that the author published a spin off series from this book. If you read the last book (Lost in</span>
  <span id="freeText9980221731464226978" style="display:none">This is the last book in the Blue Blood series. I have adored these books from the very first one. But as the series started to get further in number, the books started to lack their usual luster. Plots started to get shaky, and some things were simply forgotten. Some of the books were so cliche and typical that you felt angered that such a beautiful and interesting plot got ruined. <br /><br />First complaint was that the author published a spin off series from this book. If you read the last book (Lost in Time), you know that one of the main characters, Bliss, was sent to go find the Hell Hounds. So here I was, expecting that the book would get published before this book was released. Long behold, I found out that Bliss' adventures only made it onto the NOOK. So if you don't possess a NOOK or were aware of such events, you started this novel off a tad bit confused. An author shouldn't go from 6 or so books in physical copy and then throw a major section of it into the digital were most readers can not obtain it. VERY sloopy on the authors part. <br /><br />Second, the plot became predictable. You knew exactly what was going to happen to Mimi and Jack, even though they were 'pledged' to Lucifier. But that isn't all. Since book 4, you are wondering what the Van Alen Legacy is, and in the final book, it is revealed. Instead of a revelation that should blow your mind to another planet, you are sitting there thinking 'that was so lame'. That seems harsh, right? But it shouldn't be. The author made all this money on other books that drew you in on the hopes on some GRAND ending to the series, but in the end, you are left with a rushed and terribly ending book.<br /><br />Third and last, the book was a build up. That, in itself, was not an error. BUT, all this action was leading up to something. As the book is slowly ending, you are looking at the remaining pages like, 'this can not end well...' And most of you will be correct. In the last 50 pages, there is a hasty battle, a horrible ending, and you left with frustration. <br /><br />BUT, the book still has some good plots with it. Gripping plot, but this book missed a lot of the main concepts from the others. And the ending to this book leaves you hanging. For whatever reason, I'm not sure. Find out for yourself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9980221731464226978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_527246346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527246346" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2641242-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582995922p2/2641242.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527246346?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/2641242-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781907411502" href="/book/show/17126291-the-gates-of-paradise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2641242-leah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2641242-leah?shelf=books-read-2016">books-read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527246346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14489026379399090468">So, I have finally finished the Blue Bloods series. And it was such an amazing finale. I wrote in my review of Lost In Time that I expected good things from this finale, and it didn't let me down. Yes, I would have liked a bigger battle (or a longer battle I think I mean) but all the build up to the battle was amazing. It was like a chess match, and everyone on the good side were just getting all their pieces in place to defeat the big bad and it was pretty freaking epic.<br/><br/>Schuyler is one of those</span>
  <span id="freeText14489026379399090468" style="display:none">So, I have finally finished the Blue Bloods series. And it was such an amazing finale. I wrote in my review of Lost In Time that I expected good things from this finale, and it didn't let me down. Yes, I would have liked a bigger battle (or a longer battle I think I mean) but all the build up to the battle was amazing. It was like a chess match, and everyone on the good side were just getting all their pieces in place to defeat the big bad and it was pretty freaking epic.<br /><br />Schuyler is one of those unforgettable characters. I loved her from the word go, and she's just remained so strong throughout, anybody would crumble under what Schuyler goes through, but she doesn't. She knows what she has to do and she does it, this is her destiny, her legacy and she's not about to let anything get in the way, not even Jack leaving. Bliss is back, which is amazing. I wasn't a fan of the way she abruptly left the series, and I haven't read Wolf Pact, which seems to have been a bit of a failed series, as there's only the one book. I may go back and read it, I'm unsure how it filters into the Blue Bloods timeline. And Jack and Mimi are in the Underworld, ostensibly to help the good side, but with those two you just never know ;)<br /><br />Gates of Paradise is one of the most satisfying finales I've ever read. It was genuinely so good, so satisfying and it pretty much covered every single unanswered question. Nothing was left undone, except for those last few ellipses - which I assume is what leads into the new Blue Bloods books (YAY). This is truly one of the most enjoyable, well-thought out series I've ever read. De la Cruz is an exceptional world builder, and this was a world you could truly get lost in, because it's so different to our own. The settings were amazing, in this one they visit London, Rome, HELL!!!!!, and it never seemed forced, it all flowed so naturally. If you like young adult or supernatural books this series is a must-read, even if you don't, give it a go because it is such a fascinating series and I'm so sad it's come to an end, and so glad I finally got to the end, I still have no idea what I stopped reading, but that was a mistake as I have raced through the final three books and it's made me so happy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14489026379399090468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_362365038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362365038" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2118696-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560530332p2/2118696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362365038?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/2118696-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer362365038&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362365038" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11795831321380783822">I will admit, I've been reading this series since its inception and quite a lot of time has passed since I read #6. I also didn't get to read the .5 books, so perhaps that explains my confusion.<br/><br/>Bliss is a wolf? How the heck did that happen?!<br/><br/>I am just so confused and I don't know where to start. Not sure I got why Jack had to be such a jerk the entire book, even if it was to convince Lucifer of his loyalty. I don't understand how people whose souls were "destroyed" a la Cordelia and Dylan could s</span>
  <span id="freeText11795831321380783822" style="display:none">I will admit, I've been reading this series since its inception and quite a lot of time has passed since I read #6. I also didn't get to read the .5 books, so perhaps that explains my confusion.<br /><br />Bliss is a wolf? How the heck did that happen?!<br /><br />I am just so confused and I don't know where to start. Not sure I got why Jack had to be such a jerk the entire book, even if it was to convince Lucifer of his loyalty. I don't understand how people whose souls were "destroyed" a la Cordelia and Dylan could show up in the end in Heaven....and if Dylan was there, why couldn't Bliss be with him? Michael and Gabrielle and Lucifer and Bendix -- so confused, and I'm smart. How can Schuyler have 2 fathers? And why did Gabrielle disappear in this past incarnation? Did I miss something about her being trapped?<br /><br />Clearly, you can see that this book left me totally confuzzled and maybe didn't give me the kind of closure I wanted from the Series. The first few books were beautiful, gripping, creative, and fast-paced....and while Melissa de la Cruz achieves the pacing in this book, I just felt that it lacked the oomph from the start of the series. Schuyler and Jack were the stars of the series, and I felt their love story deserved more than a page and a half to wrap up.<br /><br />And Oliver taking Finn as a conduit? After he loathed that role? Hated that.<br /><br />So there you go -- my review for others who have finished the book. Farewell, Blue Bloods. I have no idea what just happened. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11795831321380783822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/1795202-blue-bloods-series-by-melissa-de-la-cruz-start-may-10th">Blue Bloods series by Melissa de la Cruz Start: May 10th</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MQVuuCZWZsmIastxiiipR+VQB0XC0eYVufT3qEbQ6SkWW//hbuDKvVWcntLZJciOxvj1U3gZsdx18IvgGoNoEg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5TZqAyvxGbR8UidfAxhP78jC5hZFGzKGU7V1a8ZtuAzCaPtaY0e1wKGkcvxQFS4m62oUAP/TZU+fsQkjmj45Nw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer3275188282752171559">Melissa de la Cruz is the New York Times and USA Today best-selling author of many critically acclaimed and award-winning novels for teens including The Au Pairs series, the Blue Bloods series, the Ashleys series, the Angels on Sunset Boulevard series and the semi-autobiographical novel Fresh off the Boat.<br/><br/>Her books for adults include the novel Cat’s Meow, the anthology Girls Who Like Boys Who Like</span>
  <span id="freeText3275188282752171559" style="display:none">Melissa de la Cruz is the New York Times and USA Today best-selling author of many critically acclaimed and award-winning novels for teens including The Au Pairs series, the Blue Bloods series, the Ashleys series, the Angels on Sunset Boulevard series and the semi-autobiographical novel Fresh off the Boat.<br /><br />Her books for adults include the novel Cat’s Meow, the anthology Girls Who Like Boys Who Like Boys and the tongue-in-chic handbooks How to Become Famous in Two Weeks or Less and The Fashionista Files: Adventures in Four-inch heels and Faux-Pas.<br /><br />She has worked as a fashion and beauty editor and has written for many publications including The New York Times, Marie Claire, Harper’s Bazaar, Glamour, Cosmopolitan, Allure, The San Francisco Chronicle, McSweeney’s, Teen Vogue, CosmoGirl! and Seventeen. She has also appeared as an expert on fashion, trends and fame for CNN, E! and FoxNews.<br /><br />Melissa grew up in Manila and moved to San Francisco with her family, where she graduated high school salutatorian from The Convent of the Sacred Heart. She majored in art history and English at Columbia University (and minored in nightclubs and shopping!).<br /><br />She now divides her time between New York and Los Angeles, where she lives in the Hollywood Hills with her husband and daughter. </span>

Indee<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText65031941954911361\" style=\"display:none\">When the Mayflower set sail in 1620, it carried on board the men and women who would shape America: Miles Standish; John Alden; Constance Hopkins. But some among the Pilgrims were not pure of heart; they were not escaping religious persecution. Indeed, they were not even human. They were vampires.\nThe vampires assimilated quickly into the New World. Rising to levels of enormous power, wealth, and influence, they were the celebrated blue bloods of American society. \n\nThe Blue Bloods vowed that their immortal status would remain a closely guarded secret. And they kept that secret for centuries. But now, in New York City, the secret is seeping out. Schuyler Van Alen is a sophomore at a prestigious private school. She prefers baggy, vintage clothes instead of the Prada and pearls worn by her classmates, and she lives with her reclusive grandmother in a dilapated mansion. Schuyler is a loner...and happy that way. Suddenly, when she turns fifteen, there is a visible mosaic of blue veins on her arm.
